## APPENDIX 2: GENERAL FOOD SAFETY CONSIDERATIONS

Eating food contaminated with certain bacteria, viruses, parasites or contains harmful toxins can cause foodborne illnesses. These illnesses are usually acute, occurring within 1 to 36 hours after consuming the contaminated or poisonous food. The symptoms typically last from 1 to 7 days and include one or more of the following symptoms: abdominal pain, diarrhea, vomiting, feeling sick, dehydration and collapsing. Foods that are most likely to contain harmful bacteria or viruses fall into two categories:

1. Uncooked fresh vegetables and fruits
2. Some animal products, such as unpasteurized (raw) milk; soft cheeses made with raw milk; ȝɞȯ ɰȝʋ ɣɰ ɿɞȯȳɰȩɣɣɕȳȯ ȳȿȿɴʳ ɰȝʋ ʟɴɄʳ ɰȝʋ ɴɄȳɗɗʟɴɄʳ ɰȝʋ ɭɣɿɗɻɰʑʳ ɰȝʋ ɝȳȝɻʳ ȝɞȯ ɻɄȳɇɰ juices; luncheon meats and deli-type salads (without added preservatives)

While most children who develop a foodborne illness will get better without medical interventions, it is advisable to consult with the doctor if symptoms are severe or persist for more than a week.

Preparing and consuming safe foods starts at the time of food purchase. Box 1 outlines a few tips to assist you in shopping for safe food for your children.

### Box 1. Tips for safe food purchase

- Purchase food from reliable sources.
- Read the 'Product Label' for food safety information on all foods and beverages.
- Put raw seafood, poultry, or meat in separate plastic bags.
- Pick up perishable foods last, and plan to go directly home from the grocery store.
- Buy only pasteurized milk, soft cheeses made with pasteurized milk, and pasteurized juices that have been treated to control harmful bacteria.
- Always purchase refrigerated eggs.
- Do not buy food displayed in unsafe or unclean conditions.
- Always check the expiry date of the food to be purchased:
- o A 'Sell-By' or 'Expiry (EXP)' date tells the store how long to display the product for sale. Y ou should buy the product before the date expires.
- ɣ Ơ ˑƫȳɴɻ ǊȾ Ȁɴȳȯ ƫʑ ˉɣɰ ƫȳȾɣɰȳˊ˒ ȯȝɻȳ ɇɴ ɰȳȩɣɝɝȳɞȯȳȯ Ⱦɣɰ ɻɄȳ Ȩȳɴɻ ʠȝʊɣɰ ɣɰ ɯɿȝɗɇɻʑʲ Ǌɻ ɇɴ not a purchase or safety date.
- o A 'Use-By' date is the last date recommended for product use while at peak quality. The date has been determined by the manufacturer of the product.

![Picture 327](images/SRC013/picture-327.png)

Ǥɞȩȳ ʑɣɿ ɭɿɰȩɄȝɴȳ ɻɄȳ Ⱦɣɣȯʳ ɇɻ ɇɴ ɇɝɭɣɰɻȝɞɻ ɻɣ Ⱦɣɗɗɣʋ ɴɭȳȩɇʟȩ ɭɰȝȩɻɇȩȳɴ ɻɄȝɻ ensure  proper  handling  and  consumption.  These  practices  fall  under  the following  four  categories: Clean,  Separate,  Cook  and  Chill .  More  details about  these  practices  are  outlined  in  Box  2 [48] .

### Box 2. Tips for proper food handling

#### Clean:

#### Separate:

![Picture 328](images/SRC013/picture-328.png)

- Wash your hands before, during, and after food preparation and consumption.
- Wash your hands with soap for at least 60 seconds.
- Practice good personal hygiene during food handling and preparation activities.
- Ƭɗȳȝɞ ʑɣɿɰ ɕɇɻȩɄȳɞʷ ǖȳȳɭ ȝɗɗ Ⱦɣɣȯ ɭɰȳɭȝɰȝɻɇɣɞ ɭɰȳɝɇɴȳɴ ȩɗȳȝɞʵ ʋȝɴɄ ȩɣɿɞɻȳɰɴʳ tabletops, cooking surfaces and the sink with hot, soapy water before you cook and after they come into contact with raw seafood, poultry, meat, eggs ɣɰ ʠɣɿɰʲ
- Ƭɗȳȝɞ ʑɣɿɰ Ⱦɣɣȯʷ ȌȝɴɄ ʊȳȿȳɻȝȨɗȳɴ ȝɞȯ Ⱦɰɿɇɻɴ ʋɇɻɄ ȩɗȳȝɞ ʋȝɻȳɰ ȨȳȾɣɰȳ ɭȳȳɗɇɞȿʲ Vinegar may also be used to disinfect vegetables and fruits.
- Limit washing eggs, raw meat and poultry since washing causes bacteria to spread faster. Instead, pat the eggs with a clean, damp towel and the raw meat and poultry with a separate damp towel as well.
- Wipe food packaging with soap and water before opening, especially the lids of cans and jars.
- Keep cooked and ready-to-eat foods away from raw seafood, poultry, meat, and eggs in the refrigerator while cooking. Juices from raw seafood, poultry, meats and cracked eggs can contaminate ready-to-eat foods, so it is important to separate them.
- Ensure that cooked and ready-to-eat foods are placed on top shelves, while raw foods are placed on lower shelves in the refrigerator in order to prevent the transfer of bacteria from raw foods to cooked foods.
- If possible, use separate sets of knives, cutting boards, and utensils for seafood, poultry, meat, and eggs. Ensure to wash them in hot, soapy water or in the dishwasher between uses.
- Plates that touch raw foods are not safe to reuse for cooked foods until they have been washed. Use clean plates to hold cooked foods, and wash plates thoroughly in hot, soapy water after they touch raw foods.

![Picture 329](images/SRC013/picture-329.png)

![Picture 330](images/SRC013/picture-330.png)

| Cook:   | • Use clean water. • Cook all food thoroughly: • The cooking temperature needs to reach at least 75º C or above to ensure the food is safe and free from all pathogenic bacteria. • Afood thermometer must be used to measure the internal temperature of cooked foods. Check the internal temperature in several places to make sure that the seafood, poultry, meat, or egg product is cooked to safe minimum internal temperatures. • For microwave or oven cooking: always cover food, stir, and rotate for even cooking. • Consume leftovers within 3-4 days. • Reheat leftovers only once. If leftovers are not consumed after being reheated, throw them out.   |
|---------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| Chill:  | • ǖȳȳɭ ɻɄȳ ɻȳɝɭȳɰȝɻɿɰȳ ɣȾ ʑɣɿɰ ɰȳȾɰɇȿȳɰȝɻɣɰ Ȩȳɗɣʋ ̻̰Ƭʳ ȝɞȯ ɻɄȝɻ ɣȾ ʑɣɿɰ Ⱦɰȳȳʗȳɰ Ȩȳɗɣʋ ˅ ̷̰̾Ƭʲ Ǯɰɣɭȳɰ ɻȳɝɭȳɰȝɻɿɰȳɴ Ʉȳɗɭ ɴɗɣʋ ɻɄȳ ȿɰɣʋɻɄ ɣȾ ɄȝɰɝȾɿɗ bacteria. • Do not keep food at room temperature for more than 2 hours.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |

There are a few general guidelines that will help reduce the risk of foodborne illnesses:

- Protect food from insects, rodents, and other animals.
- Store non-perishable food products in a cool and dry place.
- Ʋɣ ɞɣɻ ɣʜȳɰ Ⱦɣɣȯɴ ɣɰ Ȩȳʊȳɰȝȿȳɴ ȩɣɞɻȝɇɞɇɞȿ ɰȝʋ ȳȿȿɴ ɿɞɭȝɴɻȳɿɰɇʗȳȯ ɝɇɗɕʳ ȝɞȯ ɿɞɭȝɴɻȳɿɰɇʗȳȯ fruit juice.
- You cannot tell by looking, smelling, or even tasting a food whether it contains pathogens. Yet these pathogens-like disease causing bacteria, viruses, or parasites, can make you sick.
- You should never taste food to determine if it is safe to eat.

![Picture 331](images/SRC013/picture-331.png)

![Picture 336](images/SRC013/picture-336.png)

Healthy diets are important at every age. This chapter focuses on toddlers aged 2-3 years and preschoolers aged 3-5 years. Toddlers and preschoolers are very receptive and impressionable, which gives you the perfect opportunity to help them establish healthy eating habits. Although toddlers and preschoolers have a slower growth compared to infants, they still need enough energy to fuel their active play and enough nutrients to support their growth and development.

![Picture 337](images/SRC013/picture-337.png)

## Assessment of Child's Weight and Height

It  is  important  that  a  doctor  or  healthcare  provider  monitors  the  growth  of  your  child  by measuring his/her weight, height, and head circumference (for children under 24-36 months). The doctor will later draw these measurements on the appropriate growth charts in order to assess  your  child's  growth  and  development.

### What are growth charts?

- Growth  charts are graphic presentations that illustrate the distribution of body measurements in children (weight, height, head circumference, body mass index (BMI)).
- Growth  charts  are  the  most  useful  tool  for  assessing  growth  and  nutritional  status  in children.
- The use of the appropriate growth charts may identify abnormal trends in growth that can be indicative of poor nutrition or the presence of disease.

#### In some instances, the measurements may reveal certain growth-related problems, such as:

- The child has a low weight for his/her age (underweight or severely underweight): This may be the result of the child being too thin or too short for his/her age. It may be the result of poor nutrition or certain illnesses. Underweight children are more vulnerable to diseases and may experience delays in their development.
- The child is short for his/her age (stunted or severely stunted): If your child's height is below the normal range for his/her age (a condition referred to as stunting), this may be the result of long-term malnutrition or illness. It has consequences on the physical development of the child and is often accompanied by poor mental development.
- The child has lost weight (wasted or severely wasted): This may occur because of poor nutrition or illness. Wasted children have a higher risk of contracting diseases and illnesses.
- ǼɄȳ ȩɄɇɗȯ  ɇɴ  ɣʊȳɰʋȳɇȿɄɻ  ɣɰ  ɣȨȳɴȳʴ  Ȓ ɣɿɞȿ  ȩɄɇɗȯɰȳɞ  ȩȝɞ  Ȩȳȩɣɝȳ  ɣʊȳɰʋȳɇȿɄɻ  ɣɰ  ɣȨȳɴȳ  Ⱦɣɰ ȯɇʜȳɰȳɞɻ ɰȳȝɴɣɞɴʲ ǼɄȳ ɝɣɴɻ Ⱦɰȳɯɿȳɞɻ ȩȝɿɴȳ ɇɴ ɣʊȳɰȾȳȳȯɇɞȿʳ ɿɞɄȳȝɗɻɄʑ Ⱦȳȳȯɇɞȿ ɭɰȝȩɻɇȩȳɴʳ genetic factors (i.e., running in the family), or a combination of all these factors. In rare cases, obesity in children may result from a medical condition, which is diagnosed by the doctor. Overweight and obesity early in life can increase the risk of obesity and chronic diseases later in life.
- The child has a larger-than-normal or smaller-than-normal head circumference: This helps in assessing brain size as an indicator of possible developmental or nutritional problems.

![Picture 338](images/SRC013/picture-338.png)

Box  1  below  summarizes  the  health  and  social  implications  associated  with  overweight  and obesity, as well as those associated with the child being underweight, wasted, or stunted [ 1,  2] .

Box 1. Implications associated with overweight and obesity, as well as those associated with underweight, wasting, and stunting among 2-5-year-old children

#### Overweight and obesity

#### Underweight, wasting, and stunting

- Social problems including bullying
- ƫɰȳȝɻɄɇɞȿ ȯɇʝȩɿɗɻɇȳɴ ɴɿȩɄ ȝɴ ȝɴɻɄɝȝ ȝɞȯ ɴɗȳȳɭ ȝɭɞȳȝ
- Lower quality of life
- Type  2  diabetes,  high  blood  pressure,  high  blood  cholesterol,  and cardiovascular  diseases  later  in  life
- Joints and bone problems
- Social problems including bullying
- Delayed mental growth and reduced intellectual capacity
- Poor school performance
- Increased risk of infections and illness
- Ǳɇɴɕ ɣȾ ɝɣɰɻȝɗɇɻʑʳ ɴɭȳȩɇʟȩȝɗɗʑ ɇɞ ɴȳʊȳɰȳ ȩȝɴȳɴ

## Dietary Recommendations

Ǥʜȳɰ ʑɣɿɰ ȩɄɇɗȯ ȝ ʊȝɰɇȳɻʑ ɣȾ Ⱦɣɣȯɴ Ⱦɰɣɝ ɻɄȳ ɴɇʐ Ⱦɣɣȯ ȿɰɣɿɭɴʲ ȌɄȳɞ ȯȳȩɇȯɇɞȿ ɣɞ ʋɄɇȩɄ Ⱦɣɣȯ ɣɰ Ȩȳʊȳɰȝȿȳ ɻɣ ɣʜȳɰ ʑɣɿɰ ȩɄɇɗȯʳ ȩɄɣɣɴȳ ɣɭɻɇɣɞɴ ɻɄȝɻ ȝɰȳ ɰɇȩɄ ɇɞ ɞɿɻɰɇȳɞɻɴ ȝɞȯ ɗɇɝɇɻȳȯ ɇɞ ɴɿȿȝɰʳ ɴȝɗɻʳ and unhealthy fats [3] .

ǼȝȨɗȳ ̷ Ȩȳɗɣʋ ɭɰɣʊɇȯȳɴ ʑɣɿ ʋɇɻɄ ɴɣɝȳ ɭɰȝȩɻɇȩȝɗ ɻɇɭɴ ɣɞ Ʉɣʋ ɻɣ ɣʜȳɰ ȝɞ ȝȯȳɯɿȝɻȳ ȝɞȯ Ȩȝɗȝɞȩȳȯ diet to your child [4] ʲ Ȓɣɿ ȩȝɞ ȝɗɴɣ ȩɄȳȩɕ Appendix 1 for the number of servings from each food group per day.

| Food groups   | What to include                             | Practical tips                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              |
|---------------|---------------------------------------------|-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| Vegetables    | All fresh, frozen, and dried vegetables     | • Make vegetables part of your child's daily meals • Ǥʜȳɰ ʑɣɿɰ ȩɄɇɗȯ ɄȳȝɗɻɄʑ ɴɞȝȩɕɴ ɴɿȩɄ ȝɴ ȩȝɰɰɣɻ sticks or cucumber slices, cherry tomatoes, among others • Choose a variety of colorful vegetables to provide ʑɣɿɰ ȩɄɇɗȯ ʋɇɻɄ ȯɇʜȳɰȳɞɻ ʊɇɻȝɝɇɞɴ ȝɞȯ ɝɇɞȳɰȝɗɴ • Favor fresh or frozen vegetables over canned vegetables, since the canned varieties contain a lot of salt |
| Fruits        | All fresh, frozen, canned, and dried fruits | • Favor whole fruits instead of fruit juices (if juice is ɣʜȳɰȳȯʳ ȩɄɣɣɴȳ ̷̶̶̉ ȾɰȳɴɄ ɭȝɴɻȳɿɰɇʗȳȯ ɒɿɇȩȳɴ ȝɞȯ ensure the quantity does not exceed ½ cup which is 125 mL) • Ǥʜȳɰ ʑɣɿɰ ȩɄɇɗȯ ʋɄɣɗȳ Ⱦɰɿɇɻɴ ȝɴ ȝ ɴɞȝȩɕ ȝɻ ɴȩɄɣɣɗ or at home • Choose a variety of colorful fruits to provide your ȩɄɇɗȯ ʋɇɻɄ ȯɇʜȳɰȳɞɻ ʊɇɻȝɝɇɞɴ ȝɞȯ ɝɇɞȳɰȝɗɴ                                            |

## Fluid Intake Recommendations

Ȓɣɿɰ  ȩɄɇɗȯ  ɞȳȳȯɴ  ȝȯȳɯɿȝɻȳ  ʠɿɇȯ  ɇɞɻȝɕȳ  ɻɣ  ɰȳɝȝɇɞ  ʋȳɗɗ˅Ʉʑȯɰȝɻȳȯʲ  ƫȳɗɣʋ  ȝɰȳ  ɻɄȳ  ȿȳɞȳɰȝɗ  ʠɿɇȯ recommendations  according  to  your  child's  age [6] :

- 2-3-year-old: 4 cups (1 L) from water (and other beverages).
- 4-5-year-old: 5 cups (1.25 L) from water (and other beverages).
* 1 cup = 250 mL

If you were told by a doctor that your child is underweight or obese, then make sure to consult ʋɇɻɄ ʑɣɿɰ ȯɇȳɻɇɻɇȝɞ ɣɰ ɭɄʑɴɇȩɇȝɞ Ⱦɣɰ ȝɞ ȳʐȝȩɻ ȩȝɗȩɿɗȝɻɇɣɞ ɣȾ ɻɄȳɇɰ ʠɿɇȯ ɞȳȳȯɴʲ

### When choosing beverages other than water, be aware that:

- Sugar-sweetened  beverages  such  as  carbonated  soft  drinks  and  fruit  drinks  should  be limited. These are high in added sugars, which can contribute to tooth decay and weight gain,  while  also  replacing  other  more  nutritious  beverages  such  as  milk.
- Fruits are rich in natural sugars. Hence, fresh fruit juices are high in nutrients but are also ɄɇȿɄ ɇɞ ɴɿȿȝɰʳ ʋɄɇȩɄ ȩȝɞ ȩɣɞɻɰɇȨɿɻȳ ɻɣ ʋȳɇȿɄɻ ȿȝɇɞʲ ǼɄȳɰȳȾɣɰȳʳ ɇɻ ɇɴ ɇɝɭɣɰɻȝɞɻ ɻɣ ɣʜȳɰ ȝ maximum of one serving (125 mL- half a cup) of fresh fruit juice (with no added sugar) to your child per day.

![Picture 343](images/SRC013/picture-343.png)

## How to Boost My Child's Immunity

Children need adequate intakes of nutrients and vitamins to help boost their immune system and protect them against infections. However, there are no magical foods or supplements that will boost your child's immune system [7] . The best advice for supporting your child's immunity is ɞɣɻ ɻɣ Ⱦɣȩɿɴ ɣɞ ɴɭȳȩɇʟȩ ɞɿɻɰɇȳɞɻɴʳ Ȩɿɻ ɰȝɻɄȳɰ ɻɣ ɗɣɣɕ ȝɻ ɻɄȳɇɰ ɣʊȳɰȝɗɗ ȯɇȳɻȝɰʑ ɇɞɻȝɕȳ ȝɞȯ ɴɻɰɇʊȳ Ⱦɣɰ ȝ diet that is varied and balanced which consists of food and beverages from the six food groups. Prioritize foods that are nutrient-rich such as vegetables and fruits which supply an abundant amount of antioxidants, vitamins, and minerals. Make sure to also limit their consumption of processed  foods,  snacks  and  foods  that  are  high  in  sugar,  salt,  and  unhealthy  fats.  Review Appendix 1 for details pertinent to dietary recommendations for your child.

![Picture 344](images/SRC013/picture-344.png)

![Picture 345](images/SRC013/picture-345.png)

Many children go through a phase of refusing certain food types, especially when trying new foods. These children are known as 'picky eaters'. This behavior tends to occur especially in ʑɣɿɞȿ ȩɄɇɗȯɰȳɞ ˉɿɞȯȳɰ ʟʊȳ ʑȳȝɰɴ ɣȾ ȝȿȳˊʳ Ȩɿɻ ɇɻ ȩȝɞ ȝɗɴɣ Ʉȝɭɭȳɞ ȝɻ ȝɞʑ ɻɇɝȳ [8, 9] . It is the child's way of showing you their independence; it is also considered a normal phase of growing up. If ʑɣɿɰ ȩɄɇɗȯ ɇɴ ɭȝɴɴɇɞȿ ɻɄɰɣɿȿɄ ȝ ɭɇȩɕʑ ȳȝɻɇɞȿ ɭɄȝɴȳʳ ʑɣɿ ɝȝʑ Ȩȳ ʟɞȯɇɞȿ ɇɻ ʊȳɰʑ Ⱦɰɿɴɻɰȝɻɇɞȿ ȝɞȯ stressful. But you need to know that picky eating rarely causes any serious nutritional, medical or growth problems for the child, and it is a phase that most children grow out of it [8] .

ǵɣɝȳ ȩɄɇɗȯɰȳɞ Ʉȝʊȳ ɝɣɰȳ ȯɇʝȩɿɗɻ ȳȝɻɇɞȿ ɄȝȨɇɻɴʳ ȝɞȯ ɻɄȳʑ ȩȝɞ Ȩȳ ȩɣɞɴɇȯȳɰȳȯ ȝɴ ˑȳʐɻɰȳɝȳ ɭɇȩɕʑ eaters.' In these cases, professionals may consider this as a feeding disorder, and you will need the help of a health professional to help your child grow out of it. The section below explains the ȯɇʜȳɰȳɞȩȳ Ȩȳɻʋȳȳɞ ɭɇȩɕʑ ȳȝɻȳɰɴ ȝɞȯ ȳʐɻɰȳɝȳ ɭɇȩɕʑ ȳȝɻȳɰɴ [8] .

## Picky eaters &amp; Extreme picky eaters

Extreme picky eating can last for a longer time as compared to picky eating. Extreme picky eaters can grow out of it over months or years; however, this usually needs to be done with the help of a health professional [8] . Extreme picky eating is usually more common in children with social communication disorders [8] .

Although being a picky eater usually is harmless, being an extreme picky eater can cause serious ɭɰɣȨɗȳɝɴ ɴɿȩɄ ȝɴ ȿɰɣʋɻɄ ɭɰɣȨɗȳɝɴʳ ɞɿɻɰɇɻɇɣɞȝɗ ȯȳʟȩɇȳɞȩɇȳɴʳ ȯȳɄʑȯɰȝɻɇɣɞ ȝɞȯ ɣɻɄȳɰ ȩɣɞȯɇɻɇɣɞɴ [8] . Table 2 provides you with a direct comparison between the two behaviors.

![Picture 346](images/SRC013/picture-346.png)

|                                       | Picky eating                                                                                                                                                                                                                | Extreme picky eating                                                                                                                                      |
|---------------------------------------|-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| How common is it?                     | • Very common in children. • Ơʜȳȩɻɴ ̷ʿ̹ ɣȾ ȩɄɇɗȯɰȳɞ ȝȿȳȯ ̷˅̻ years.                                                                                                                                                             | • Less common. • More common in children with social communication disorders.                                                                             |
| Health/Growth consequences            | • No health/growth consequences or only minor ones.                                                                                                                                                                         | • Moderate to severe health/growth consequences. • But, in some cases, there is no health/growth consequences or only minor ones.                         |
| Impact on parents                     | • Can be very stressful for parents.                                                                                                                                                                                        | • Usually very stressful for parents.                                                                                                                     |
| Do children grow out of it?           | • Usually, children grow out of it within a period of weeks to months.                                                                                                                                                      | • Can take a longer time (months or years) for children to grow out of it. • Management requires the help of a health professional.                       |
| Eating habits                         | • They eat a range of food items, with a preference for some food items from each food group. • On some days, they may only eat very little amounts, or they may Ʉȝʊȳ ɭɰȳȾȳɰȳɞȩȳɴ Ⱦɣɰ ȝ ɴɭȳȩɇʟȩ narrow range of food types. | • They eat a limited range of food ɇɻȳɝɴʳ ɿɴɿȝɗɗʑ ɗȳɴɴ ɻɄȝɞ ̸̶ ȯɇʜȳɰȳɞɻ types. • They often exclude some food groups altogether.                            |
| Feelings towards new food items       | • Picky eaters are upset when new food items are introduced and their Ⱦȝʊɣɰɇɻȳ Ⱦɣɣȯ ɇɴ ɞɣɻ ɣʜȳɰȳȯʲ                                                                                                                          | • Extreme picky eaters are upset whennewfooditemsareintroduced and when their favorite food is not ɣʜȳɰȳȯ ȝɞȯ ɿɴɿȝɗɗʑ ɻɄȳɇɰ ɰȳȝȩɻɇɣɞ can be more extreme. |
| Hiding food in other food items       | • Ȓɣɿ ȩȝɞ ɴɣɝȳɻɇɝȳɴ Ʉɇȯȳ ɻɄȳ refused food item in other foods that the child likes.                                                                                                                                         | • ǼɄɇɴ ɇɴ ɝɣɰȳ ȯɇʝȩɿɗɻ ɻɣ Ȩȳ ȯɣɞȳ because the child can detect it.                                                                                        |
| Ȍɣɿɗȯ ɻɄȳʑ ȳȝɻ ɣʜȳɰȳȯ food if hungry? | • They would eventually eat the ɣʜȳɰȳȯ Ⱦɣɣȯʳ ȝɞȯ ʋɣɿɗȯ ɞɣɻ ɴɻȝɰʊȳ themselves.                                                                                                                                               | • ǼɄȳʑ ʋɇɗɗ ɞɣɻ ȳȝɻ ɻɄȳ ɣʜȳɰȳȯ Ⱦɣɣȯ usually, and they may be at risk of being ill from starving themselves [8] .                                          |

![Picture 347](images/SRC013/picture-347.png)

### When to seek professional help?

Do not get frustrated if your child is a picky eater. Just provide your child with healthy food choices and try your best to help your child grow out of this phase. In fact, most picky eaters remain healthy, and their eating habits tend to improve gradually as they get older [10] . If your ȩɄɇɗȯ˔ɴ ɭɇȩɕʑ ȳȝɻɇɞȿ ɇɴ ɞɣɻ ȝʜȳȩɻɇɞȿ ɻɄȳɇɰ ɄȳȝɗɻɄ ɣɰ ȿɰɣʋɻɄʳ ɻɄȳɞ ɻɄȳɰȳ ɇɴ ɞɣ ɞȳȳȯ ɻɣ Ȩȳ ȩɣɞȩȳɰɞȳȯʲ Ǉɣʋȳʊȳɰʳ ʋɄȳɞ ʑɣɿɰ ȩɄɇɗȯ˔ɴ ȳȝɻɇɞȿ ɄȝȨɇɻɴ ȝɰȳ ȝʜȳȩɻɇɞȿ ɻɄȳɇɰ ɄȳȝɗɻɄʳ  ȿɰɣʋɻɄʳ ɣɰ ɇɴ ɴɻɰȳɴɴɇɞȿ ʑɣɿ ȝɴ ȝ ɭȝɰȳɞɻʳ ɻɄȳɞ ʑɣɿ ɴɄɣɿɗȯ ɴȳȳɕ ɭɰɣȾȳɴɴɇɣɞȝɗ Ʉȳɗɭ ɻɣ ʟɞȯ ɻɄȳ ɝɣɴɻ ɴɿɇɻȝȨɗȳ ȝɭɭɰɣȝȩɄ ɻɣ ɣʊȳɰȩɣɝȳ this problem [8] .

Box 2 provides you with some useful steps to follow if your child is a picky eater [8] .

![Picture 348](images/SRC013/picture-348.png)

![Picture 349](images/SRC013/picture-349.png)

![Picture 350](images/SRC013/picture-350.png)

![Picture 351](images/SRC013/picture-351.png)

Mothers tend to get worried when their child eats very little, refuses to eat a meal or refuses to eat healthy foods like fruits and vegetables [11] ʲ ǁɣɰ ɴɣɝȳ ɝɣɻɄȳɰɴʳ ɻɄɇɴ ʋɣɰɰʑ ȩȝɞ Ȩȳ ɴɇȿɞɇʟȩȝɞɻʳ especially if the child is underweight or not gaining weight adequately. For others, unconsumed meals can be a source of frustration, especially when the parents do not like to waste food that has been prepared, or when they believe that children have to 'clean their plates' [11] .  As a result, parents may end up forcing their child to eat their entire meal.

It is true that the child may end up eating a bit more when being forced to eat. However, studies have shown that the act of forcing the child to eat can cause long-term problems for the child, which are summarized below:

- Disliking or avoiding certain foods. This can be the result of a negative experience of Ȩȳɇɞȿ Ⱦɣɰȩȳȯ ɻɣ ȳȝɻ ȝ ɴɭȳȩɇʟȩ Ⱦɣɣȯʲ ƬɄɇɗȯɰȳɞ ȝɰȳ ɇɞ Ⱦȝȩɻ ȝȨɗȳ ɻɣ ɝȝɕȳ ɯɿɇȩɕ ȝɴɴɣȩɇȝɻɇɣɞɴ between foods and unpleasant experiences that  may  accompany them [ 11] .
- Disturbing  the  child's  ability  to  respond  to  their  internal  feelings  of  hunger  and fullness. This  means that the child would not listen to his/her body and so food intake becomes determined by other factors other than what the body requires. Instead, the child learns to continue eating, even when they feel full, stopping only when the plate is empty [ 11] .
- Development of overeating and overweight. As explained above, forcing the child to eat can disturb the child's ability to learn appropriate appetite control. This can eventually lead to overeating and the development of overweight and obesity [11] .

Except in rare cases, children are usually extremely good at knowing when they are full, and ʋɄȳɞ ɻɄȳʑ ȝɰȳ Ʉɿɞȿɰʑʲ ǼɄȳɰȳȾɣɰȳʳ ɇɻ ɇɴ ɇɝɭɣɰɻȝɞɻ ɻɄȝɻ ʑɣɿ ɻɰɿɴɻ ʑɣɿɰ ȩɄɇɗȯ ȝɞȯ Ȩȳ ȩɣɞʟȯȳɞɻ that they will eat when feeling hungry. It is also important to remember that children have a natural tendency to reject new foods and this should not be met with pressure. Instead, continue ɣʜȳɰɇɞȿ Ⱦɣɣȯɴ ȝɞȯ ȝȩȩȳɭɻ ɻɄȝɻ ȩɄɇɗȯɰȳɞ ɝȝʑ ɰȳȾɿɴȳ ɻɣ ȳȝɻ ɇɻʳ ȝɴ ɻɄɇɴ ɇɴ ȝ ɞɣɰɝȝɗ ɭȝɰɻ ɣȾ ɻɄȳɇɰ development. Also remember that the stomachs of young children are smaller than adults' and you may be serving too much food that your child cannot consume.

## Vegetarian Children

Some families will choose to limit meat consumption or follow a vegetarian diet for health or ɭȳɰɴɣɞȝɗ ɰȳȝɴɣɞɴʲ Ơ ʊȳȿȳɻȝɰɇȝɞ ȯɇȳɻ ɇɴ ȯȳʟɞȳȯ ȝɴ ɻɄȳ ȩɣɞɴɿɝɭɻɇɣɞ ɣȾ ɭɰɇɝȝɰɇɗʑ ɣɰ ɣɞɗʑ ɭɗȝɞɻ˅ based foods (such as vegetables, fruits, cereals and starchy vegetables, legumes, unsalted, raw nuts and seeds), and usually excludes some or all foods from the animal-based food items such ȝɴ ˉɝɇɗɕʿȯȝɇɰʑ ɭɰɣȯɿȩɻɴʳ ʟɴɄʳ ɭɣɿɗɻɰʑʳ ɝȳȝɻ ȝɞȯ ȳȿȿɴˊʲ

If you choose this dietary pattern for your child, you should consult with a doctor or dietitian ɻɣ ɝȝɕȳ ɴɿɰȳ ɻɄȝɻ ʑɣɿɰ ȩɄɇɗȯ ɇɴ ɣȨɻȝɇɞɇɞȿ ȝȯȳɯɿȝɻȳ ȝɝɣɿɞɻɴ ɣȾ ȝɗɗ ɞɿɻɰɇȳɞɻɴʲ ǵȩɇȳɞɻɇʟȩ ȳʊɇȯȳɞȩȳ suggests that, if done properly, and if monitored by a healthcare provider, vegetarian diets can meet the nutrient requirements of young children [12-14] .

![Picture 352](images/SRC013/picture-352.png)

![Picture 353](images/SRC013/picture-353.png)

![Picture 354](images/SRC013/picture-354.png)

Since foodborne illness are very common if foods are not properly stored in the lunchbox, or consumed at the right temperature, you need to follow some safety guidelines [15] :

- For foods that should be kept cold, you might need to use an insulated bag with some sort ɣȾ ȝ ȩɣɗȯ ɴɣɿɰȩȳ ˉɇȩȳ ɣɰ ȿȳɗ ɭȝȩɕɴ ɇɞ ɻɄȳ ɇɞɴɿɗȝɻȳȯ Ȩȝȿ ʋɇɗɗ ȯɣˊʲ Ȓ ɣɿ ɝɇȿɄɻ ȩɰȳȝɻȳ ʑɣɿɰ ɣʋɞ reusable cold source by simply adding a frozen water bottle or container to the lunchbox.
- Avoid giving your child hot meals especially if the daycare/school does not have the option of heating foods. Remember that meals should be heated up to a safe temperature before being consumed.

For a healthy child's lunchbox, follow the below guidelines (Box 3) [16] .

| Box 3. Guidelines to follow when preparing your child's lunchbox   | Box 3. |--------------------------------------------------------------------|----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| Choices                                                            | • Fill the lunchbox as such: • ́ ɣȾ ɇɻ ʋɇɻɄ ̸˅̹ ȯɇʜȳɰȳɞɻ ɕɇɞȯɴ ɣȾ ȩɣɗɣɰȾɿɗ ʊȳȿȳɻȝȨɗȳɴ ȝɞȯ Ⱦɰɿɇɻɴ • ¼ of it with whole grain cereals • ¼ofit with healthy proteins (legumes, turkey breast, unsalted, raw nuts/seeds) • Add milk and/or dairy products to the main meal or snacks (such as a 200 mL pack of pasteurized milk). |

![Picture 355](images/SRC013/picture-355.png)

Safe preparation and handling of food are essential to reduce the susceptibility of toddlers and preschoolers to foodborne illnesses and food poisoning.

Refer to Appendix 2 for general food safety guidelines.

![Picture 356](images/SRC013/picture-356.png)

![Picture 357](images/SRC013/picture-357.png)

ǁɣɣȯ ȝɗɗȳɰȿʑ ɇɴ ȯȳʟɞȳȯ ȝɴ ȝɞ ȝȨɞɣɰɝȝɗ ɰȳɴɭɣɞɴȳ ɣȾ ɻɄȳ Ȩɣȯʑ ɻɣ ȝ ȩȳɰɻȝɇɞ Ⱦɣɣȯ ɣɰ Ȩȳʊȳɰȝȿȳ [17] . ǵɻɿȯɇȳɴ ɴɿȿȿȳɴɻ ɻɄȝɻ ȝɰɣɿɞȯ ̻̉ ɣȾ ȩɄɇɗȯɰȳɞ ɿɞȯȳɰ ɻɄȳ ȝȿȳ ɣȾ ʟʊȳ ʑȳȝɰɴ Ʉȝʊȳ Ⱦɣɣȯ ȝɗɗȳɰȿɇȳɴ [ 17 , 18] .  The majority of children who have milk, egg, wheat or soy allergies would outgrow these ȝɗɗȳɰȿɇȳɴʲ  Ǉɣʋȳʊȳɰʳ  ɣɻɄȳɰ  ȝɗɗȳɰȿɇȳɴ  ɴɿȩɄ  ȝɴ  ɻɰȳȳ˅ɞɿɻɴʳ  ɭȳȝɞɿɻɴʳ  ʟɴɄ  ȝɞȯ  ɴɄȳɗɗʟɴɄ  ȝɗɗȳɰȿɇȳɴ  ȝɰȳ usually  lifelong [ 17 ,  19] .

Food allergy is not the same as food intolerance, although the two terms are often mixed up. ǼɄȳ ɝȝɇɞ ȯɇʜȳɰȳɞȩȳ ɇɴ ɻɄȝɻ Ⱦɣɣȯ ɇɞɻɣɗȳɰȝɞȩȳ ˉɴɿȩɄ ȝɴ ɗȝȩɻɣɴȳ ɇɞɻɣɗȳɰȝɞȩȳˊ ȯɣȳɴ ɞɣɻ ɇɞʊɣɗʊȳ ɻɄȳ immune system, whereas food allergies cause an immune system reaction [17] . The symptoms of food intolerance are usually less serious and are often limited to digestive problems. In contrast, Ⱦɣɣȯ ȝɗɗȳɰȿɇȳɴ ȩȝɞ ȩȝɿɴȳ ȝ ʋɇȯȳ ɰȝɞȿȳ ɣȾ ɴʑɝɭɻɣɝɴ ɻɄȝɻ ȝʜȳȩɻ ɞɿɝȳɰɣɿɴ ɣɰȿȝɞɴ ɇɞ ɻɄȳ Ȩɣȯʑ ȝɞȯ that can vary in their degree of severity. In some cases, allergic reactions may be very severe and life-threatening.

## What are the most common allergens in the diet?

Ơɰɣɿɞȯ ̶̿̉ ɣȾ ȝɗɗ Ⱦɣɣȯ ȝɗɗȳɰȿɇȳɴ ȝɰȳ ȩȝɿɴȳȯ Ȩʑ ɻɄȳ Ⱦɣɗɗɣʋɇɞȿ ɻʑɭȳɴ ɣȾ Ⱦɣɣȯɴ [17, 20] :

- Animal-based milk such as cow's milk
- Eggs
- Peanuts
- Soy
- Tree nuts
- Fish
- ǵɄȳɗɗʟɴɄ ˉȩɰɿɴɻȝȩȳȝɞɴ ȝɞȯ ɝɣɗɗɿɴȩɴˊ
- Wheat
- Seeds

ǼɄȳɰȳ ɇɴ ɞɣ ɞȳȳȯ ɻɣ ȝʊɣɇȯ ȝɞʑ ɣȾ ɻɄȳɴȳ Ⱦɣɣȯɴʳ ɿɞɗȳɴɴ ʑɣɿɰ ȩɄɇɗȯ ɇɴ ȝɗɗȳɰȿɇȩʲ Ƭɿɻɻɇɞȿ ɣʜ ȝ ɝȝɒɣɰ Ⱦɣɣȯ ȿɰɣɿɭ ȩȝɞ ɗȳȝȯ ɻɣ ɞɿɻɰɇȳɞɻ ȯȳʟȩɇȳɞȩɇȳɴʳ ɴɣ ȝɗʋȝʑɴ ȩɣɞɴɿɗɻ ʋɇɻɄ ȝ ȯɣȩɻɣɰ ɭɰɇɣɰ ɻɣ ȳɗɇɝɇɞȝɻɇɞȿ ȝɞʑ type of food from your child's diet [20] .

Some individuals can have allergies for food additives including colors and preservatives, but usually allergic reactions from ordinary food items are more common [20] .

![Picture 358](images/SRC013/picture-358.png)

## What are the symptoms of food allergies?

An allergic reaction can begin within minutes to an hour after ingesting the food or beverage that ɻɄȳ ȩɄɇɗȯ ɇɴ ȝɗɗȳɰȿɇȩ ɻɣʲ ƶȝȩɄ ȩɄɇɗȯ ɝȝʑ ȳʐɭȳɰɇȳɞȩȳ Ⱦɣɣȯ ȝɗɗȳɰȿʑ ȯɇʜȳɰȳɞɻɗʑ ȝɞȯ ɝɇȿɄɻ Ʉȝʊȳ ɣɞȳ ɣɰ more symptoms. The most common symptoms of food allergy are [17] :

- Diarrhea
- Vomiting
- Cough
- Swelling
- Dry and itchy skin (eczema)
- Itching or swelling of the lips, tongue, or mouth
- Itching or tightness in the throat
- Skin rashes
- Sore, red and/or itchy eyes
- Runny or blocked nose
- Lowered blood pressure
- Stomach cramps and pain
- Red itchy bumps on the skin (hives)
- Trouble breathing or shortness of breath
- Wheezing (coarse sound when breathing)

In some cases, severe allergic reaction may occur which is known as 'anaphylaxis'; this can be life-threating [20,21] ȝɞȯ ɇɴ ɿɴɿȝɗɗʑ ɝȝɞɇȾȳɴɻȳȯ Ȩʑ ȨɰȳȝɻɄɇɞȿ ȯɇʝȩɿɗɻɇȳɴ ȝɞȯ Ⱦȝȩȳ ɴʋȳɗɗɇɞȿʲ ǊȾ ɴɿȩɄ ɴʑɝɭɻɣɝɴ ȯȳʊȳɗɣɭʳ ʑɣɿɰ ȩɄɇɗȯ ʋɇɗɗ ɞȳȳȯ ɇɝɝȳȯɇȝɻȳ ɝȳȯɇȩȝɗ ȝɻɻȳɞɻɇɣɞʲ Ǽɰȳȳ ɞɿɻɴʳ ɭȳȝɞɿɻɴʳ ʟɴɄʳ ȝɞȯ ɴɄȳɗɗʟɴɄ ɿɴɿȝɗɗʑ ȩȝɿɴȳ ɻɄȳ ɝɣɴɻ ɴȳʊȳɰȳ ɰȳȝȩɻɇɣɞɴ ȩɣɝɭȝɰȳȯ ɻɣ ɣɻɄȳɰ ȩɣɝɝɣɞ ȝɗɗȳɰȿȳɞɴ [17] .

## How do we diagnose a food allergy?

Ơ ȯɇȝȿɞɣɴɇɴ ɴɄɣɿɗȯ Ȩȳ ȯɣɞȳ Ȩʑ ȝ ȯɣȩɻɣɰʲ Ȓɣɿ ɴɄɣɿɗȯ ɞɣɻ ɝȝɕȳ ɻɄȳ ȯɇȝȿɞɣɴɇɴ ʑɣɿɰɴȳɗȾ ɻɣ ȝʊɣɇȯ ȝɞʑ unnecessary dietary restrictions. In case a food allergy is diagnosed, you must have a dietary plan to replace the eliminated food items, and you also need to have a plan in case of emergency [19] . If your child develops any of the typical allergy-related symptoms after eating any type of food or beverage, you should immediately contact a doctor.

![Picture 359](images/SRC013/picture-359.png)

![Picture 360](images/SRC013/picture-360.png)

## Nutritional concerns in children with food allergies

It  is  important  to  keep  in  mind  that  eliminating  a  certain  food  group  (because  of  an  allergy) ʋɇɻɄɣɿɻ  ɰȳɭɗȝȩɇɞȿ  ɇɻ  Ȩʑ  ɻɄȳ  ɰɇȿɄɻ  ȝɗɻȳɰɞȝɻɇʊȳ  ȩȝɞ  ȩȝɿɴȳ  ɞɿɻɰɇɻɇɣɞȝɗ  ȯȳʟȩɇȳɞȩɇȳɴ  ȝɞȯ  ȿɰɣʋɻɄ problems in your child [22] . For example, milk, eggs and soy are good sources of fat and protein. ƶɗɇɝɇɞȝɻɇɞȿ ɻɄȳɴȳ Ⱦɣɣȯ ɇɻȳɝɴ Ȩȳȩȝɿɴȳ ɣȾ Ⱦɣɣȯ ȝɗɗȳɰȿɇȳɴ ɝɇȿɄɻ ɗȳȝȯ ɻɣ ɇɞɴɿʝȩɇȳɞɻ ȝɝɣɿɞɻɴ ɣȾ protein and fat in the diet if they are not replaced by other good sources [22] .

- Ʋɇȳɻɴ ɻɄȝɻ Ʉȝʊȳ ɇɞɴɿʝȩɇȳɞɻ ȝɝɣɿɞɻɴ ɣȾ Ⱦȝɻ ȯɣ ɞɣɻ ɿɴɿȝɗɗʑ ȩɣɞɻȝɇɞ ȝȯȳɯɿȝɻȳ ȝɝɣɿɞɻɴ ɣȾ energy (calories) and certain vitamins, which can lead to poor growth.
- Diets that are low in protein may also lead to protein malnutrition and hence poor growth [22] .

Another example is wheat. This cereal provides the body with carbohydrates, which are known to be an important source of energy for your child's body, and particularly the brain. Wheat also contains important vitamins and minerals. So if the child is allergic to wheat, other alternative ɴɄɣɿɗȯ Ȩȳ ɇɞȩɗɿȯȳȯ ɇɞ ʑɣɿɰ ȩɄɇɗȯ˔ɴ ȯɇȳɻ ɻɣ ɗɇɝɇɻ ȝɞʑ ɞɿɻɰɇɻɇɣɞȝɗ ȯȳʟȩɇȳɞȩɇȳɴ [22] .

Another potential challenge is that children that have one or more food allergies might experience some dietary behavior problems more than other children. For example, they may develop 'food aversion' (i.e. refusing certain types of food) or a state of anxiety about food, which again can lead to inadequate food intake [22] .

This is why it is very important that the doctor monitors the growth of children with food allergies [22] .  It  is  also  important that the doctor or dietitians provide you with the right alternatives to ɰȳɭɗȝȩȳ ɻɄȳ ȳɗɇɝɇɞȝɻȳȯ Ⱦɣɣȯɴ ȝɞȯ Ʉȳɞȩȳ ɭɰȳʊȳɞɻ ɞɿɻɰɇɻɇɣɞȝɗ ȯȳʟȩɇȳɞȩɇȳɴ [22] .    Supplements may sometimes be prescribed by the doctor when needed [22] .

## What should I do if my child was diagnosed with a food allergy?

ǼɄȳɰȳ ɇɴ ɞɣ ȩɿɰȳ Ⱦɣɰ Ⱦɣɣȯ ȝɗɗȳɰȿɇȳɴʵ ɻɄȳ ʟɰɴɻ ɴɻȳɭ ɻɄȝɻ ɝɿɴɻ Ȩȳ ȯɣɞȳ ɇɴ ɻɣ ȩɣɝɭɗȳɻȳɗʑ ȝʊɣɇȯ ɻɄȳ food or beverage that causes the allergic reaction [17, 19, 21, 23] . It is therefore important to get the help of a dietitian to plan an adequate, healthy and balanced diet for your child, to avoid any ɝɇȩɰɣɞɿɻɰɇȳɞɻ ɣɰ ɝȝȩɰɣɞɿɻɰɇȳɞɻ ȯȳʟȩɇȳɞȩɇȳɴ ȩȝɿɴȳȯ Ȩʑ ȳɗɇɝɇɞȝɻɇɞȿ ȩȳɰɻȝɇɞ Ⱦɣɣȯɴ [23] .  Below are some practical tips that can help you in managing your child's food allergy:

- Check  with  a  dietitian  and  a  doctor  to  identify  food  alternatives  or  even  nutritional ɴɿɭɭɗȳɝȳɞɻɴ  ɻɣ  ȝʊɣɇȯ  ȝɞʑ  ȯȳʟȩɇȳɞȩɇȳɴ [17] .
- Ơɗʋȝʑɴ ɰȳȝȯ Ⱦɣɣȯ ɗȝȨȳɗɴ ȝɞȯ ɗɇɴɻ ɣȾ ɇɞȿɰȳȯɇȳɞɻɴ ȨȳȾɣɰȳ ɣʜȳɰɇɞȿ ʑɣɿɰ ȩɄɇɗȯ ȝɞʑ ɞȳʋ ɇɻȳɝ [19] .
- Educate your family (at home) and teachers (in the school or nursery) about your child's allergies and what to do in case of an emergency [19] .
- If  the doctor has prescribed any medications in case of an allergic reaction, always keep those medications at hand [17] .
- ƶȝɰɗʑ  ȝɞȯ  ɯɿɇȩɕ  ɇȯȳɞɻɇʟȩȝɻɇɣɞ  ɣȾ  ɻɄȳ  ɴɇȿɞɴ  ȝɞȯ  ɴʑɝɭɻɣɝɴ  ȩȝɞ  ɭɰȳʊȳɞɻ  ɝɣɰȳ  ɴȳɰɇɣɿɴ complications  caused  by  food  allergies [21] .

![Picture 361](images/SRC013/picture-361.png)

ǵɣɝȳ ȯɣȩɻɣɰɴ ɝȝʑ ɰȳȩɣɝɝȳɞȯ ɻɄȳ ɰȳɇɞɻɰɣȯɿȩɻɇɣɞ ɣȾ ɻɄȳ ɴɭȳȩɇʟȩ Ⱦɣɣȯɴ ɻɄȝɻ Ʉȝʊȳ ȩȝɿɴȳȯ ɻɄȳ allergies, after a certain amount of time to evaluate whether the child has outgrown the allergy. Some allergies may in fact be outgrown with time and the foods may end up being tolerated after reaching the age of three or four years old. This must be done under the doctor's supervision [17] .

## Tips when dining out of the house:

As a parent of a child with one or more food allergies, it can be challenging to eat out of the house. The following tips can help you:

- Check the menu online before going to the restaurant.
- Read and/or ask about the ingredients before ordering any dish.
- Let the server be aware of your child's allergy and ensure there is no cross-contamination when preparing your child's dish.
- ǘɇɝɇɻʳ ɇȾ ɭɣɴɴɇȨɗȳʳ Ȩɿʜȳɻ˅ɴɻʑɗȳ ɰȳɴɻȝɿɰȝɞɻɴ ɻɣ ȝʊɣɇȯ ȝɞʑ ȩɰɣɴɴ˅ȩɣɞɻȝɝɇɞȝɻɇɣɞ ɻɄȝɻ ȩȝɞ Ʉȝɭɭȳɞ Ⱦɰɣɝ ɿɴɇɞȿ ɻɄȳ ɴȝɝȳ ɿɻȳɞɴɇɗɴ Ⱦɣɰ ȯɇʜȳɰȳɞɻ ȯɇɴɄȳɴʲ
- ǘɇɝɇɻ Ⱦɣɣȯɴ ɻɄȝɻ ȝɰȳ ȩɣɣɕȳȯ ɇɞ ɣɇɗʳ ȝɴ ɻɄȳʑ ɝȝʑ ɿɴȳ ɻɄȳ ɴȝɝȳ ɣɇɗ ɻɣ Ⱦɰʑ ɴȳʊȳɰȝɗ ȯɇʜȳɰȳɞɻ dishes [17] .

## Food allergy card:

Having a food allergy card can help your child and especially help the people around them (if you ȝɰȳ ɞɣɻ ȝɰɣɿɞȯˊ ɻɣ Ȩȳ ȝʋȝɰȳ ɣȾ ɻɄȳ Ⱦɣɣȯɴ ɻɄȝɻ ɴɄɣɿɗȯ ɞɣɻ Ȩȳ ɣʜȳɰȳȯ ɻɣ ɻɄȳɝʲ ǼɄȳ ȩȝɰȯ ɴɄɣɿɗȯ Ȩȳ with the child at all times, including at the school or nursery, or when the child is visiting a friend, at a party and/or in a restaurant. Inform any adult in charge that the child has this card, such as the teacher at the school or nursery the parents of the friend that your child is visiting [17] .

### The food allergy card should contain the following information:

- The name of the child
- Food items your child is allergic to
- What to do in case of emergency
- Parent's name and phone number

This card can be easily done at home (below is the card template).

![Picture 362](images/SRC013/picture-362.png)

![Picture 363](images/SRC013/picture-363.png)

Proper oral health among children paves the way for good health and wellbeing as they grow older. Early childhood is the most convenient time for your child to acquire healthy habits since at this age, they would have started to drink and eat on their own. Unhealthy diets and improper oral health habits may increase your child's risk of dental decays, especially if your child engages in the following behaviors [24] :

- Regular  and  frequent  consumption  of  sugary  foods  like  cakes,  biscuits,    candies,  and chocolates
- Regular  and  frequent  consumption  of  sugar-sweetened  beverages  like  fruit  juices  and carbonated  soft  drinks  (i.e.,  carbonated  beverages)
- Not cleaning or brushing their teeth

Hence,  it  is  extremely  important  that  you  consider  the  below  recommendations  to  ensure adequate  oral  health  for  your  child  (Box  4) [24] .

## Box 4. Recommendations to ensure adequate oral health for your child

- Ʋɣ ɞɣɻ ɣʜȳɰ ɄɇȿɄ˅ɴɿȿȝɰ Ⱦɣɣȯɴ ɻɣ ʑɣɿɰ ȩɄɇɗȯʲ Ǌɞɴɻȳȝȯʳ ɭɰɣʊɇȯȳ ʑɣɿɰ ȩɄɇɗȯ ʋɇɻɄ ɄȳȝɗɻɄʑ ɴɞȝȩɕɴ such as vegetables, fruits, and yogurt.
- ƫɰɿɴɄ ʑɣɿɰ ȩɄɇɗȯ˔ɴ ɻȳȳɻɄ ɻʋɇȩȳ ȝ ȯȝʑʳ ʋɇɻɄ ɴɝȝɗɗ ȝɝɣɿɞɻɴ ɣȾ ʠɿɣɰɇȯȳ˅ȩɣɞɻȝɇɞɇɞȿ ɻɣɣɻɄɭȝɴɻȳ ˉ̷̶̶̶ ɭɭɝ ʠɿɣɰɇȯȳˊʲ
- Watch your child brush their teeth and help them until they have acquired good brushing techniques.
- Try to make teeth brushing fun by using a timer (2 minutes). Let them use a toothbrush with an animated character that they like; this will motivate them to brush their teeth.
- Ǟȝɕȳ ɴɿɰȳ ʑɣɿɰ ȩɄɇɗȯ ȯɰɇɞɕɴ ʋȝɻȳɰ ɻɄɰɣɿȿɄɣɿɻ ɻɄȳ ȯȝʑ ɻɣ ɝȳȳɻ ɻɄȳɇɰ ȯȝɇɗʑ ʠɿɇȯ ɇɞɻȝɕȳ recommendation.
- Ensure  your  child  is  having  regular  dental  check-ups  with  a  dentist  (at  least  every  6 months).

## Your Child's Food Choices

Every parent tries their best to ensure that their child eats healthy most of the time, but there [25] .

Food and beverage options that are advertised in the media (TV or social media) are not always nutritious or healthy for your child. In fact, most of the advertised food and beverages are high [26] . Children have a remarkable ability to remember content from these advertisements and thus they tend to develop a preference for the marketed foods [25, 27-29] .

choices? [26]

- Avoid the use of TVs and tablets or any other electronic device while eating:
- Apply this to the whole family during main meals as well as snacks.
- Eat together as a family without any distractions to promote healthy eating as well as family bonding.
- Choose children's programs without advertisements:
- Choose platforms that allow you to skip commercials, or that do not include any.
- Involve your child when buying and preparing foods:
- Children  are  willing  to  learn  about  everything  at  this  age,  and  they  enjoy  being involved in doing small tasks around the house; this is a good opportunity to teach them about healthy food and beverages and let them be part of choosing, buying, and preparing  meals  and  snacks.
- Limit screen time:
- Limit screen time to a maximum of one hour per day.
- Be a role model to your child:
- Young children will imitate their parents and view them as their role models. Be mindful of your choices. Choose healthy foods and beverages and limit your screen time to encourage your child to do the same.

![Picture 367](images/SRC013/picture-367.png)

![Picture 368](images/SRC013/picture-368.png)

![Picture 369](images/SRC013/picture-369.png)

Encourage your child to lead a healthy and active lifestyle by being involved in unstructured or structured play for a minimum of 3 hours a day [30] .

ǮɄʑɴɇȩȝɗ ȝȩɻɇʊɇɻʑ Ʉȝɴ ɝȝɞʑ Ȩȳɞȳʟɻɴ Ⱦɣɰ ʑɣɿɰ ȩɄɇɗȯʳ ɇɞȩɗɿȯɇɞȿ ɻɄȳ Ⱦɣɗɗɣʋɇɞȿ [30] :

- It promotes healthy and strong bones and muscles, while improving movement skills
- It helps maintain a healthy body weight
- It improves social and intellectual skills

Box  5  below  provides  you  with  the  physical  activity  recommendations  for  toddlers  and preschoolers [30] .

### Box 5. Physical activity guidelines for toddlers and preschoolers

- Encourage your child to enjoy a variety of activities throughout the day, such as riding the bicycle, running, jumping, and swimming.
- Make sure to use protective gear such as bicycle helmets, knee pads and chin guards, to help reduce the risk of injuries.
- Gradually increase the frequency, time, and intensity of exercising as your child is growing and developing.
- Limit long hours of inactivity by encouraging your child to move more and by making physical activity part of their daily routine. Encourage a break from sitting, every 20-30 minutes.
- Limit screen time (television, computer, phones, tablets) to less than an hour per day.

REMEMBER

![Picture 370](images/SRC013/picture-370.png)

Every child is ȯɇʜȳɰȳɞɻʵ ɻɄȳɰȳȾɣɰȳʳ ȝɗɗ activities should be based on their current physical maturity. Gradually increase frequency, intensity, and time of new physical activities to reduce the risk of injury. Accidents happen more frequently when your child gets tired or due to missing protective gear.

## Importance of Adequate Sleep

Adequate  sleep  plays  a  major  role  in  modulating  the  health  and  wellbeing  of  your  child. Ǌɞɴɿʝȩɇȳɞɻ ɴɗȳȳɭ ɝȝʑ ɇɞȩɰȳȝɴȳ ɻɄȳ ɰɇɴɕ ɣȾ ɣʊȳɰʋȳɇȿɄɻ ȝɞȯ ɣȨȳɴɇɻʑ ɇɞ ȩɄɇɗȯɄɣɣȯ [31, 32] ,  and can increase the risk of developing chronic diseases, such as hypertension, cardiovascular diseases and type II diabetes later in life [32, 33] . In addition, lack of sleep can have a negative impact on the following [33,  34] :

- Physical and mental health
- Cognitive and psychosocial development
- Alertness and attention
- Vocabulary acquisition (process of learning new words)
- Learning and memory
- Mood

Box 6 provides you with the recommendations for sleep among toddlers and preschoolers [32, 33, 35] .

### Box 6. Recommendations for sleep among toddlers and preschoolers

- Make sure that your child is getting good quality of sleep as follows:
- 11- 14 hours of sleep, including naps, for children aged 2-3 years old.
- 10-13 hours of sleep, including naps, for children aged 3-5 years old. Naps at this age become shorter; preschoolers might even stop napping.
- Establish a consistent bedtime routine. Reading a book, or having a hot warm bath can help.
- Ǟȝɕȳ ɴɿɰȳ ȝɗɗ ȳɗȳȩɻɰɣɞɇȩɴ ˉɻȳɗȳʊɇɴɇɣɞʳ ʊɇȯȳɣ ȿȝɝȳɴʳ ɻȝȨɗȳɻɴˊ ȝɴ ʋȳɗɗ ȝɴ ȨɰɇȿɄɻ ɗɇȿɄɻɴʳ ȝɰȳ ɻɿɰɞȳȯ ɣʜ ȝɻ bedtime. Let the bed be a no-screen zone.
- Make sure that the bedroom is quiet, calm and at a room temperature convenient for your child.
- Having your child put on their favorite pajamas is a good strategy to encourage them to go to bed.
- Ǥʜȳɰ  ɄȳȝɗɻɄʑ  Ȩȳȯɻɇɝȳ  ɴɞȝȩɕɴ  ˉʋȝɰɝ  ɝɇɗɕʳ  ʑɣȿɿɰɻˊ  ȝɞȯ  ȝʊɣɇȯ  ɗȝɰȿȳ  ɝȳȝɗɴ  ȝɞȯ  ɴɿȿȝɰʑ  Ⱦɣɣȯɴ  ȝɻ Ȩȳȯɻɇɝȳʳ  ȝɴ  ʋȳɗɗ  ȝɴ  ȩȝʜȳɇɞȳ˅ȩɣɞɻȝɇɞɇɞȿ  Ȩȳʊȳɰȝȿȳɴ  ˉȩɣʜȳȳʳ  ɻȳȝ  ȝɞȯ  ȩȝɰȨɣɞȝɻȳȯ  ɴɣȾɻ  ȯɰɇɞɕɴˊʲ
- Encourage your child to have a proper physical activity routine, which can help them sleep better at night. Refer to section 13.
- Do not forget proper teeth brushing before bedtime! (Refer to Section 11).

### Box 1:  Protein Foods

![Picture 391](images/SRC013/picture-391.png)

Make sure to include protein rich foods in your child's daily diet. These include legumes, ʟɴɄʳ ɭɣɿɗɻɰʑʳ ɗȳȝɞ ɝȳȝɻʳ ȝɞȯ ȳȿȿɴ ȝɞȯ ɿɞɴȝɗɻȳȯʳ ɰȝʋ ɞɿɻɴ ȝɞȯ ɴȳȳȯɴʲ

General recommendations for protein foods are 2 portions per day.

#### Examples of one portion include:

- 2-4 tablespoons of cooked beans, chickpeas or lentils
- 15-30 g of seafood, skinless chicken, and lean meats
- ½-1 ½  tablespoon of canned sardines
- ½-1 ½ tablespoon of canned tuna (in water not oil)
- ½-1 boiled egg
- 1- 2 tablespoons of chopped or ground unsalted, raw nuts or seeds
- 1- 2 tablespoons of hummus
- 1 tablespoon of peanut butter

The number of portions of protein per day increases with the child's age: 2 portions/day for toddlers aged 1-2 years; 2-5 portions for children aged 2-5 years.

## APPENDIX 2: ǂƶǟƶǱƠǘ ǁǤǤƲ ǵƠǁƶǼȒ ƬǤǟǵǊƲƶǱƠǼǊǤǟǵ

Eating food that is contaminated with certain bacteria, viruses, parasites or contains harmful toxins can cause foodborne illnesses. These illnesses are usually acute, occurring within 1 to 36 hours after the consumption of the contaminated or poisonous food. The symptoms normally last  from  1  to  7  days  and  include  one  or  more  of  the  following  symptoms:  abdominal  pain, diarrhea, vomiting, feeling sick, dehydration and collapsing. Foods that are most likely to contain harmful bacteria or viruses fall into two categories:

1. Uncooked fresh vegetables and fruits
2. Some animal products, such as unpasteurized (raw) milk; soft cheeses made with raw milk; ȝɞȯ ɰȝʋ ɣɰ ɿɞȯȳɰȩɣɣɕȳȯ ȳȿȿɴʳ ɰȝʋ ʟɴɄʳ ɰȝʋ ɴɄȳɗɗʟɴɄʳ ɰȝʋ ɭɣɿɗɻɰʑʳ ɰȝʋ ɝȳȝɻʳ ȝɞȯ ɻɄȳɇɰ juices; luncheon meats and deli-type salads (without added preservatives)

While the majority of children who develop a foodborne illness will get better without medical interventions, if symptoms are severe or persist for more than a week, it is advisable to consult with a doctor.

Preparing and consuming safe foods starts at the time of food purchase. Box 1 outlines a few tips to assist you in shopping for safe food for your children.

![Picture 392](images/SRC013/picture-392.png)

### Box 1. Tips for safe food purchase

- Purchase food from reliable sources.
- Read the 'Product Label' for food safety information on all foods and beverages.
- Put raw seafood, poultry, or meat in separate plastic bags.
- Pick up perishable foods last, and plan to go directly home from the grocery store.
- Buy  only  pasteurized  milk,  soft  cheeses  made  with  pasteurized  milk,  and  pasteurized juices  that  have  been  treated  to  control  harmful  bacteria.
- Always purchase refrigerated eggs.
- Do not buy food displayed in unsafe or unclean conditions.
- Always check the expiry date of the food to be purchased:
- o A 'Sell-By' or 'Expiry (EXP)' date tells the store how long to display the product for ɴȝɗȳʲ Ȓɣɿ ɴɄɣɿɗȯ Ȩɿʑ ɻɄȳ ɭɰɣȯɿȩɻ ȨȳȾɣɰȳ ɻɄȳ ȯȝɻȳ ȳʐɭɇɰȳɴʲ
- ɣ Ơ ˑƫȳɴɻ ǊȾ Ȁɴȳȯ ƫʑ ˉɣɰ ƫȳȾɣɰȳˊ˒ ȯȝɻȳ ɇɴ ɰȳȩɣɝɝȳɞȯȳȯ Ⱦɣɰ Ȩȳɴɻ ʠȝʊɣɰ ɣɰ ɯɿȝɗɇɻʑʲ Ǌɻ ɇɴ not a purchase or safety date.
- o A 'Use-By' date is the last date recommended for the use of the product while at peak quality. The date has been determined by the manufacturer of the product.

Ǥɞȩȳ ʑɣɿ ɭɿɰȩɄȝɴȳ  ɻɄȳ  Ⱦɣɣȯʳ  ɇɻ  ɇɴ  ɇɝɭɣɰɻȝɞɻ  ɻɣ  Ⱦɣɗɗɣʋ  ɴɭȳȩɇʟȩ  ɭɰȝȩɻɇȩȳɴ  ɻɄȝɻ  ȳɞɴɿɰȳ  ɭɰɣɭȳɰ handling  and  consumption.  These  practices  fall  under  the  following  four  categories: Clean, Separate, Cook and Chill .  More  details  about  these  practices  are  outlined  in  Box  2 [37] .

![Picture 393](images/SRC013/picture-393.png)

![Picture 394](images/SRC013/picture-394.png)

| Box 2. Tips for proper food handling   | Box 2. Tips for proper food handling                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          |
|----------------------------------------|---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| Clean:                                 | • Wash your hands, before, during and after food preparation and consumption. • Wash your hands for at least 60 seconds. • Practice good personal hygiene during food handling and preparation activities. • Clean your kitchen! Keep all food preparation premises clean; wash counters, tabletops, cooking surfaces and the sink with hot, soapy water before you cook and after they come into contact with raw seafood, ɭɣɿɗɻɰʑʳ ɝȳȝɻʳ ȳȿȿɴ ɣɰ ʠɣɿɰʲ • Clean your food! Wash vegetables and fruits with clean water, before peeling. Vinegar may also be used to disinfect vegetables and fruits. • Limit washing eggs, raw meat and poultry since washing causes bacteria to spread faster. Instead, pat the eggs with a clean, damp towel, and the raw meat and poultry with a separate damp towel as well. • Wipe food packaging with soap and water before opening, especially lids of cans and jars. |
| Separate:                              | • Keep cooked and ready-to-eat foods away from raw seafood, poultry, meat, and eggs in the refrigerator and while cooking. (Juices from raw seafood, poultry, meats and cracked eggs can contaminate ready-to-eat foods, so it is important to separate them.) • Ensure that cooked and ready-to-eat foods are placed on top shelves, while raw foods are placed on lower shelves in the refrigerator, in order to prevent the transfer of bacteria from the raw foods to the cooked foods. • If possible, use separate sets of knives, cutting boards, and utensils for seafood, poultry, meat, and eggs. Ensure to wash them in hot, soapy water or in the dishwasher between uses. • Plates that touch raw foods are not safe to reuse for cooked foods until they have been washed. Use clean plates to hold cooked foods, and wash plates thoroughly in hot, soapy water after they touch raw foods.     |

![Picture 395](images/SRC013/picture-395.png)

| Cook:   | • Use clean water. • Cook all food thoroughly: • The cooking temperature needs to reach at least 75º C or above to ensure the food is safe and free from all pathogenic bacteria. • Afood thermometer must be used to measure the internal temperature of cooked foods. Check the internal temperature in several places to make sure that the seafood, poultry, meat, or egg product is cooked to safe minimum internal temperatures. • For microwave or oven cooking: always cover food, stir, and rotate for even cooking. • Consume leftovers within 3-4 days. • Reheat leftovers only once. If leftovers are not consumed after being reheated, throw them out.   |
|---------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| Chill:  | • ǖȳȳɭ ɻɄȳ ɻȳɝɭȳɰȝɻɿɰȳ ɣȾ ʑɣɿɰ ɰȳȾɰɇȿȳɰȝɻɣɰ Ȩȳɗɣʋ ̻̰Ƭʳ ȝɞȯ ɻɄȝɻ ɣȾ ʑɣɿɰ Ⱦɰȳȳʗȳɰ Ȩȳɗɣʋ ˅ ̷̰̾Ƭʲ Ǯɰɣɭȳɰ ɻȳɝɭȳɰȝɻɿɰȳɴ Ʉȳɗɭ ɴɗɣʋ ɻɄȳ ȿɰɣʋɻɄ ɣȾ harmful bacteria. • Do not keep food at room temperature for more than 2 hours.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |

![Picture 396](images/SRC013/picture-396.png)

## Choose Healthy Fats and Limit Your Child's Intake of Sugar and Salt

Your child's meals and snacks at home as well as their lunchbox should include nutritious food ɣɭɻɇɣɞɴ Ⱦɰɣɝ ɻɄȳ ɴɇʐ Ⱦɣɣȯ ȿɰɣɿɭɴ ȝɞȯ ɰȳʠȳȩɻ ɻɄȳ ɭɰɇɞȩɇɭɗȳɴ ɣȾ ɄȳȝɗɻɄʑ ȳȝɻɇɞȿ ɣɿɻɗɇɞȳȯ ɇɞ ɻɄȳ ǰȝɻȝɰ Dietary Guidelines [1] . This means that you need to limit foods that are high in sugar, salt, and unhealthy fats in your child's diet.

Many children consume excessive amounts of added sugar from sweetened foods and beverages, which can lead to dental caries and increase their risk for overweight and obesity [2, 3] . Excessive intakes of salt in children may also increase their predisposition to develop hypertension later in life [4] . While infants and toddlers need a higher fat intake compared to older children or adults, it is important that they consume healthy types of fats and oils, and reduce their intake of saturated fat, and hydrogenated and trans-fat. This chapter provides you with information and practical tips on how to choose healthy fats for your child and reduce their intake of added sugar and salt.

![Picture 401](images/SRC013/picture-401.png)

![Picture 402](images/SRC013/picture-402.png)

While sugars can be naturally occurring in certain foods (such as fruits, fruit juices, milk and dairy products), they can also be added to food during processing [5] . Consuming excessive amounts of added sugars adds calories with no nutritional value. In fact, excess intakes have been associated with  increased  risk  of  weight  gain,  high  triglycerides  levels,  insulin  resistance,  cardiovascular diseases and dental caries, while also being linked with reduced bone strength [2, 3] . Their intake should therefore be reduced to a maximum of 10% of your child's energy intake [5-7] .

Box 1 provides you with some practical tips to limit your child's intake of sweetened foods and beverages [1, 3, 8] .

### Box 1. Practical tips to limit the intake of sweetened foods and beverages

- Provide your child with three main meals and two nutritious snacks to avoid temptations to eat high sugar foods due to hunger.
- Encourage your child to snack on fresh vegetables, fruits, dates, and yogurt.
- Restrict  your  child's  consumption  of  carbonated  soft  drinks,  carbonated  and  sugar-sweetened beverages.
- Ơʊɣɇȯ ɣʜȳɰɇɞȿ ȳɞȳɰȿʑ ȯɰɇɞɕɴ ɻɣ ʑɣɿɰ ȩɄɇɗȯʲ Ǌɞ ȝȯȯɇɻɇɣɞ ɻɣ Ȩȳɇɞȿ ɄɇȿɄ ɇɞ ɴɿȿȝɰʳ ɻɄȳɴȳ ȯɰɇɞɕɴ ȝɗɴɣ ȩɣɞɻȝɇɞ ɄɇȿɄ ȝɝɣɿɞɻɴ ɣȾ ȩȝʜȳɇɞȳʳ ʋɄɇȩɄ ȩȝɞ ɗȳȝȯ ɻɣ ȯȳɄʑȯɰȝɻɇɣɞʳ ɇɞɴɣɝɞɇȝʳ ȝɞȯ ɇɞȩɰȳȝɴȳȯ Ʉȳȝɰɻ ɰȝɻȳʲ
- ƶɞȩɣɿɰȝȿȳ ʑɣɿɰ ȩɄɇɗȯ ɻɣ ɰȳɭɗȝȩȳ ɻɄȳ ɴɿȿȝɰ˅ɴʋȳȳɻȳɞȳȯ Ȩȳʊȳɰȝȿȳɴ ʋɇɻɄ ʋȝɻȳɰʳ ɗȝȨȝɞʳ ɿɞʠȝʊɣɰȳȯ ɝɇɗɕ or fresh fruit juices (in moderation - ½ a cup per day).
- If your child is reluctant to accept regular milk, blend fresh fruits or dates with the milk.
- ǘɇɝɇɻ ʑɣɿɰ ȩɄɇɗȯ˔ɴ ȩɣɞɴɿɝɭɻɇɣɞ ɣȾ ɻɰȝȯɇɻɇɣɞȝɗ ǰȝɻȝɰɇ ɴʋȳȳɻɴ ˉɴɿȩɄ ȝɴ ɴȝȿɄɣ ȝɞȯ ɗɿɯȝɇɝȝɻˊʳ Ǟɇȯȯɗȳ˅ Eastern  sweets  (such  as  basboosah  and  baklava)  as  well  as  cakes,  desserts,  chocolates  and confectioneries  (candies,  lollipops,  chewing  gum,  and  jellies).
- ǊȾ  Ʉɣɝȳɝȝȯȳ ȯȳɴɴȳɰɻɴ ɴɿȩɄ ȝɴ Ȁɝɝ Ơɗɇʳ ɝɿɄȝɗɗȝȨɇʑȝʳ ɴȝȿɄɣ ȝɞȯ ɰɇȩȳ ɭɿȯȯɇɞȿ ȝɰȳ ɣʜȳɰȳȯ ɻɣ ɻɄȳ child, make sure to prepare them  with low sugar content (and low-fat milk for children aged above two years) (small portions or lesser amounts).
- Consider using natural sources of sugar such as dates or apple sauce when preparing desserts.
- ǘȳɻ ʑɣɿɰ ȩɄɇɗȯ ȳɞɒɣʑ ɿɞɴʋȳȳɻȳɞȳȯ ȨɰȳȝɕȾȝɴɻ ȩȳɰȳȝɗɴ ɴɿȩɄ ȝɴ Ȩɰȝɞ ʠȝɕȳɴ ȝɞȯ ʋɄɣɗȳ ȿɰȝɇɞ ȩȳɰȳȝɗɴʳ instead  of  sugar  or  chocolate-coated  cereals.

![Picture 403](images/SRC013/picture-403.png)

![Picture 404](images/SRC013/picture-404.png)

![Picture 405](images/SRC013/picture-405.png)

## Reading nutrition labels:

- ǁɣɣȯɴ ȝɰȳ ȩɗȝɴɴɇʟȳȯ ȝȩȩɣɰȯɇɞȿ ɻɣ ɻɄȳɇɰ ɴȝɗɻʿɴɣȯɇɿɝ ȩɣɞɻȳɞɻʳ ȝɴ Ⱦɣɗɗɣʋɴʴ
- High: contains more than 1.5g of salt (or 600mg of sodium) per 100g of food.
- Medium: contains more than 0.3g and up to 1.5g of salt (120mg - 600 mg of sodium) per 100g of food.
- Low: contains 0.3g or less of salt (120 mg of sodium) per 100 g of food.
- ƫȳʊȳɰȝȿȳɴ ȝɰȳ ȩɗȝɴɴɇʟȳȯ ȝȩȩɣɰȯɇɞȿ ɻɣ ɻɄȳɇɰ ɴȝɗɻ ȩɣɞɻȳɞɻ ȝɴ Ⱦɣɗɗɣʋɴʴ
- High: contains more than 0.75g of salt (300mg of sodium) per 100 mL.
- Medium: contains more than 0.3g and up to 0.75g of salt (120mg - 300mg of sodium) per 100mL.
- Low: contains 0.3g or less of salt (120mg of sodium) per 100mL.
- Refer to section 5 below for more information on nutrition labels.

![Picture 406](images/SRC013/picture-406.png)

![Picture 407](images/SRC013/picture-407.png)

Healthy fats are needed for proper growth and development of infants and young children [5, 12] . Ǉɣʋȳʊȳɰʳ ȳʐȩȳɴɴ ɇɞɻȝɕȳɴ ɣȾ ɴȝɻɿɰȝɻȳȯ Ⱦȝɻɴ ȝɞȯ Ʉʑȯɰɣȿȳɞȝɻȳȯʿɻɰȝɞɴ˅Ⱦȝɻɴ ȝɰȳ ɿɞɄȳȝɗɻɄʑ Ⱦɣɰ ʑɣɿɰ child and can increase their risk of developing chronic diseases later in life [5] .

Low-fat diets are NOT recommended for children under the age of two years! [1, 13] Low-fat diets are not appropriate for young children, particularly those under two years, because they are still in their growing phase. Unless the child has an allergy, full-fat milk, yogurt and cheese should be given to children until they are two years old.

![Picture 408](images/SRC013/picture-408.png)

### Box 3 below presents practical tips to choose healthy fats and oils, while reducing saturated fat ȝɞȯ ȝʊɣɇȯɇɞȿ Ʉʑȯɰɣȿȳɞȝɻȳȯʿɻɰȝɞɴ˅Ⱦȝɻɴ [5, 8, 9, 13, 14] .

### Box 3. Practical tips to choose healthy fats and oils

- Encourage  your  child  to  consume  healthy  fats  from  olives,  avocados,  tahini,  unsalted,  raw  nuts ˉȳʐȝɝɭɗȳʴ ʋȝɗɞɿɻɴˊ ȝɞȯ ɴȳȳȯɴ ˉȳʐȝɝɭɗȳʴ ɭɿɝɭɕɇɞ ɴȳȳȯɴ ȝɞȯ ʠȝʐɴȳȳȯɴˊʳ ɣɇɗʑ ʟɴɄ ˉȳʐȝɝɭɗȳʴ ɴȝɗɝɣɞʳ sardines and light canned tuna).
- Limit your child's consumption of saturated fats which is primarily found in fatty meat, poultry skin, cold  cuts  (sausages,  salami),  processed  meats  (hotdog,  luncheon  meats),  full-fat  dairy  products, yellow cheeses, cream, butter, and tropical oils (coconut and palm oils).
- Limit  the  use  of  butter,  cream,  ghee,  and  high-fat  sauces  (mayonnaise,  salad  dressings)  when cooking and preparing food for your child. Instead, use healthy vegetable oils such as olive, canola, ȩɣɰɞ ȝɞȯ ɴɿɞʠɣʋȳɰ ɣɇɗɴ ɇɞ ɝɣȯȳɰȝɻɇɣɞʲ
- Restrict your child's consumption of foods that contain hydrogenated and trans-fats. These include margarine, shortening, commercially processed baked goods (pastries, crackers, biscuits, pies, and cakes),  fried  and  fast  foods  (French  fries,  burgers,  shawarma  and  deep-fried  falafel),  as  well  as packaged foods made with hydrogenated oils.
- ǘɇɝɇɻ ʑɣɿɰ ȩɄɇɗȯ˔ɴ ȩɣɞɴɿɝɭɻɇɣɞ ɣȾ ɻɰȝȯɇɻɇɣɞȝɗ ǰȝɻȝɰɇ ɴʋȳȳɻɴ ˉɴɿȩɄ ȝɴ ɴȝȿɄɣ ȝɞȯ ɗɿɯȝɇɝȝɻˊ ȝɞȯ Ǟɇȯȯɗȳ Eastern sweets (such as basboosah and baklava) that are high in fat. These sweets can be enjoyed on special occasions.
- Encourage your child to enjoy more homemade baked goods.
- Ǥʜȳɰ ʑɣɿɰ ȩɄɇɗȯ Ⱦɣɣȯɴ ɻɄȝɻ ȝɰȳ ɞȝɻɿɰȝɗɗʑ ɗɣʋ ɇɞ Ⱦȝɻ ɴɿȩɄ ȝɴ ʊȳȿȳɻȝȨɗȳɴʳ Ⱦɰɿɇɻɴʳ ʋɄɣɗȳ ȿɰȝɇɞ ȩȳɰȳȝɗɴʳ ɇɞ addition to low-fat versions of milk, yogurt and laban, since the full-fat versions are high in saturated fat (for children aged above two years).
- Ǥʜȳɰ ʑɣɿɰ ȩɄɇɗȯ  ɝɣɰȳ  ʋɄɇɻȳʳ  ɗɣʋ˅Ⱦȝɻ  ȝɞȯ  ɗɣʋ˅ɴȝɗɻ  ȩɄȳȳɴȳɴ  ˉɄȝɗɗɣɿɝɇʳ  ȝɕɕȝʋɇˊ  ɇɞɴɻȳȝȯ  ɣȾ  ʑȳɗɗɣʋʳ processed and spreadable cheeses.
- Prepare your child's foods by steaming, baking, grilling, or sautéing, rather than frying or deepfrying.
- Ǳȳɝɣʊȳ ɻɄȳ ʊɇɴɇȨɗȳ Ⱦȝɻɴ Ⱦɰɣɝ ɝȳȝɻɴ ȨȳȾɣɰȳ ɭɰȳɭȝɰɇɞȿ ȝɞȯ ɣʜȳɰɇɞȿ ɇɻ ɻɣ ʑɣɿɰ ȩɄɇɗȯʲ ȌɄȳɞ ɭɰȳɭȝɰɇɞȿ chicken or other poultry, make sure to remove the skin before cooking.
- Limit your child's intake of fast-food.
- Save high-fat and high caloric foods and desserts for special occasions only and in small portions.

![Picture 409](images/SRC013/picture-409.png)

## Reading nutrition labels:

- When  reading  the  ingredients  list,  avoid  purchasing  food  products  that  have  the  following ingredients: hydrogenated  oils or partially hydrogenated  oils.
- Choose products that do not contain trans-fat.
- ǁɣɣȯɴ ȝɰȳ ȩɗȝɴɴɇʟȳȯ ȝȩȩɣɰȯɇɞȿ ɻɣ ɻɄȳɇɰ ɴȝɻɿɰȝɻȳȯ Ⱦȝɻ ȩɣɞɻȳɞɻʳ ȝɴ Ⱦɣɗɗɣʋɴʴ
- High: contains more than 5g of saturated fat per 100g of food.
- Medium: contains more than 1.5g and up to 5g of saturated fat per 100g of food.
- Low: contains 1.5g or less of saturated fat per 100g of food.
- ƫȳʊȳɰȝȿȳɴ ȝɰȳ ȩɗȝɴɴɇʟȳȯ ȝȩȩɣɰȯɇɞȿ ɻɣ ɻɄȳɇɰ ɴȝɻɿɰȝɻȳȯ Ⱦȝɻ ȩɣɞɻȳɞɻ ȝɴ Ⱦɣɗɗɣʋɴʴ
- High: contains more than 2.5g of saturated fat per 100mL.
- Medium: contains more than 0.75g and up to 2.5g of saturated fat per 100mL.
- Low: contains less than 0.75g of saturated fat per 100mL.
- Refer to section 5 for more information on nutrition labels.

![Picture 410](images/SRC013/picture-410.png)

![Picture 411](images/SRC013/picture-411.png)

A nutrition label is a tool that will help you make informed decisions about prepackaged foods and beverages before buying them for your child. Box 4 below provides you with tips to familiarize yourself with nutrition labels [8, 15, 16] .

### Box 4. Tips to familiarize yourself with nutrition labels

### Familiarize yourself with the below terms:

Nutrition labels usually include the below components:

- Servings per container: total number of servings in the entire food package or container. Keep in mind that the food product may contain more than one serving.
- Calories: amount of energy provided by one serving of this food or beverage.
- Nutrients: total  fats  (saturated  fats  and  trans-fats),  cholesterol,  sodium,  total  carbohydrates ˉȯɇȳɻȝɰʑ ʟȨȳɰɴʳ ɻɣɻȝɗ ɴɿȿȝɰɴ ȝɞȯ ȝȯȯȳȯ ɴɿȿȝɰɴˊʳ ɭɰɣɻȳɇɞɴ ȝɞȯ ɴɣɝȳ ɝɇɞȳɰȝɗɴ ȝɞȯ ʊɇɻȝɝɇɞɴ ˉʊɇɻȝɝɇɞ Ʋʳ calcium,  iron,  and  potassium).

![Picture 412](images/SRC013/picture-412.png)

### Keep in mind the following:

#### For Food:

- Aim for less than 5g of sugar per 100g of food.
- Aim for less than 0.3g of salt per 100g of food.
- Aim for less than 3g of total fat per 100g of food.
- Aim for less than 1.5g of saturated fat per 100g of food.
- Aim for less than 0.2g of trans-fat per 100g of food.

#### For Beverages:

- Aim for less than 2.5g of sugar per 100mL of a beverage.
- Aim for less than 0.3g of salt per 100mL of a beverage.
- Aim for less than 1.5g of total fat per 100mL of a beverage.
- Aim for less than 0.75g of saturated fat per 100mL of a beverage.
- Aim for less than 0.2g of trans-fat per 100mL of a beverage.
- ƬɄɣɣɴȳ Ⱦɣɣȯɴ ɻɄȝɻ ȝɰȳ ɄɇȿɄ ɇɞ ʟȨȳɰʳ ȩȝɗȩɇɿɝʳ ȝɞȯ ɇɰɣɞʳ ʋɄɇɗȳ ɗɇɝɇɻɇɞȿ ɻɄɣɴȳ ɻɄȝɻ ȝɰȳ ɄɇȿɄ ɇɞ ɴɿȿȝɰʳ ɴȝɻɿɰȝɻȳȯ  Ⱦȝɻʳ  ȝɞȯ  ɴȝɗɻʿɴɣȯɇɿɝʲ
- The serving size on nutrition labels is usually for adults and is based on a 2000 calorie diet. The ɴȳɰʊɇɞȿ ɴɇʗȳ ɴɭȳȩɇʟȩ Ⱦɣɰ ʑɣɿɰ ȩɄɇɗȯ ʋɇɗɗ ȳʊȳɞɻɿȝɗɗʑ Ȩȳ ɴɝȝɗɗȳɰ ɻɄȝɞ ʋɄȝɻ ɇɴ ɇɞȯɇȩȝɻȳȯ ɣɞ ɻɄȳ ɭȝȩɕȝȿȳʳ depending on your child's age.

![Picture 413](images/SRC013/picture-413.png)
